The Four-Power Pact May Be Signed Today

Rome Preparing Grand Ceremony

A Prelude to the Conclusion of the Disarmament Convention

(Paris) The Four-Power Pact has been drafted and is expected to be initialed in Rome on Thursday, June 1, in the afternoon by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and the ambassadors of France, Britain, and Germany to Rome. The full text of the pact is prepared to be published simultaneously in the capitals of the four countries: Britain, France, Germany, and Italy. (Havas dispatch, 31st)

Rome: The Italian government has prepared a grand signing ceremony for the Four-Power Pact, which may be signed within 48 hours. The venue is the Palazzo Venezia, where Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and the ambassadors of Britain, France, and Germany will each sign the first letter of their names as proof. Mussolini's plan is for the major powers to guarantee each other to ensure the security of Europe. However, British Prime Minister MacDonald interprets this pact as hoping that smaller countries can also participate. Mussolini's initial proposal stipulated compelling Germany to demand the revision of the peace treaty, but it is heard that the final draft has been amended to gradually, rather than immediately, revise the peace treaty. It is recognized here that the four countries' agreement to this pact is an indication that the dispute over the British disarmament plan in Geneva has been largely resolved. There are also expectations that a disarmament convention can be agreed upon before the opening of the London World Economic Conference. (National dispatch, 29th)

France Weakens the Power of the Pact

(Paris) France is still secretly working to reduce the real value of the Four-Power Pact, hoping to adapt it to its own needs and maintain its hegemony in Europe through military alliances. A correspondent for Le Matin in Geneva reports that French Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour intends to supplement the Four-Power Pact with guarantees, and the original text of the meeting minutes contains four main points: (1) The Four-Power Pact does not harm existing treaties between France and its allied countries. (2) France cannot agree to any attempt to raise territorial issues defined by treaty revisions. (3) All procedural issues must be submitted to the League of Nations, the only appropriate international body, for resolution. (4) France will uphold the principle of unanimous agreement within the League of Nations, which should also include the countries concerned. According to Le Matin, these meeting minutes will be sent to the governments of the four contracting states and the Little Entente countries on the day the Four-Power Pact is signed. (National dispatch, 29th)

German Government Has Announced Its Support

Rome: The German government announced today its support for the full text of the Four-Power Pact, which has been accepted by Italy, France, and Britain. It also supports the application of Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant on sanctions, and the pact will be valid for ten years. The provisions of the Four-Power Pact have been revised and are currently being proofread. As for the language used in the pact, it may be in French only, or in both English and French as requested by Britain, or in all four languages: English, French, German, and Italian. In case of doubt, French will prevail. It has not yet been decided which of these three methods will be used. (Havas dispatch, 31st)

(Berlin) German officials were still expressing doubts yesterday about the impending signing of the Four-Power Pact, but this morning they appeared optimistic, saying that diplomatic negotiations were proceeding smoothly. Berlin expects the Four-Power Pact to be signed soon. (Havas dispatch, 31st)

Little Entente Countries Express Understanding

Prague, Czechoslovakia: After a meeting of the Political Standing Committee of the Little Entente countries this afternoon, a communique was issued stating that the ministers of Czechoslovakia, Yugoslavia, and Romania declared that their respective countries had exchanged ratification documents for the treaty signed by the Little Entente countries in Geneva on February 16, 1933. Regarding the Four-Power Pact, the Political Standing Committee believes that the newly proposed provisions are in line with the spirit of the memorandum submitted by the French government on April 10 of this year, namely, that the Four-Power Pact can only involve the interests of the signatory states themselves. The Political Standing Committee believes that the Four Powers have satisfied the important objections raised by the Little Entente countries, and the signatory states of the Four-Power Pact themselves recognize the limitations of what they will do. The Little Entente countries have taken note of the guarantees given by the Four Powers in this regard. The so-called limitations are: (1) The authority of the League of Nations will not be changed in any way. (2) The principle of unanimous agreement must be applied to the application of Article 19 of the League of Nations Covenant (i.e., the General Assembly of the League of Nations may at any time request member states to review treaties that are no longer applicable and consider international situations that may endanger world peace). In addition, France has also explicitly assured the Little Entente countries that the Four Powers will not make any attempts to modify the treaties based on prior agreement. Therefore, the Four-Power Pact, whether directly or indirectly, cannot become an agreement to modify the current borders of the Little Entente countries. After studying the issue of revising the territorial clauses in the peace treaties, the three ministers formally and definitively stated their views on this matter as follows: namely, that the issue of revising the current borders of the Little Entente countries will not be raised, as mentioned above. However, in principle, the three countries should still declare that any oppression of any country to force it to recognize the modification of borders will not be recognized by the Little Entente countries. Regarding the Geneva disarmament issue, the three ministers continue to hope that it will achieve concrete results. The three countries support the British disarmament plan as the basis for a future disarmament convention. They also support the principle of unifying the military systems of the European continent and the principle of reducing armaments. As for the principle of equality in armaments, it is also supported by the three countries within the scope that can guarantee the security of all countries. The Little Entente countries have also decided to firmly demand that the Disarmament Conference make detailed regulations on the effective supervision system of disarmament and entrust this power to the Permanent Disarmament Commission. (Havas dispatch, 30th)

Poland Declares Extreme Opposition

Warsaw: Political circles here declare that Poland is extremely opposed to the Four-Power Pact, and that no matter what the attitude of the Little Entente countries is, it will never allow Poland to be affected by it. (Havas dispatch, 30th)

The Soviet Union is Taking Countermeasures

Rome: Soviet Russian Ambassador to Rome, Potemkin, has departed for Geneva to meet with the Soviet Foreign Affairs Commissioner, Litvinov, before going to Moscow. It is generally believed that the Russian envoy's trip is related to the Four-Power Pact. (Havas dispatch, 30th)

Disarmament Conference to Draft a Separate Security Agreement

(Geneva) The matter discussed in today's Disarmament Conference is that after the conclusion of the future disarmament convention, a security agreement will be drafted again to conclude the Disarmament Conference. The draft agreement will include the exclusion of violence, the interpretation of aggressors, and the management of the joint responsibilities that countries should bear when one country is invaded by another and the Council of the League of Nations unanimously decides to enforce the judgment, etc., as stated in the disarmament convention. During the meeting, US Representative Davis raised the issue of whether the exclusion of violence would be applied to the whole world or only to a part of Europe. According to Davis' observation, if such matters can be universally implemented throughout the world as stated in the draft agreement, it would be quite in line with Roosevelt's suggestion. However, Roosevelt also pointed out that the first task of the Disarmament Conference is to establish an agreement for the substantial reduction of armaments. (National dispatch, 30th)

(London) Labor Party leader Lansbury made a passionate speech in the House of Commons today, asking the British government to reconsider Foreign Minister Simon's resolution announced at the Geneva Disarmament Conference that Britain would retain sky bombardment for policing purposes, and asking whether the government would not allow its attitude to be changed even if it destroyed the Disarmament Conference. Lord President Baldwin said that the government had made this resolution after repeated consideration, and had notified Parliament of this proposal last November. He could not admit that this resolution could destroy the suggestions of the Disarmament Conference. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

Contents of the Four-Power Pact

Rome: According to reliable sources, the Four-Power Pact contains an introduction and five or six articles, which mostly stipulate that the signatory states formally agree to maintain peace for ten years, and agree to resolve economic issues. The pact will mention Articles 10, 16, and 19 of the League of Nations Covenant, and recognize the equal rights of the Four Powers on disarmament, but with the understanding that such equal rights will not be implemented temporarily during the agreed time. This pact stipulates the general revision of protective tariffs and the promotion of commercial exchange, and stipulates the period for maintaining peace as ten years. The pact also specifies the method for revising the pact. News from Prague, Czechoslovakia, is that the Administrative Council of the Little Entente countries announced that France's views on the Four-Power Pact can be accepted, because the signatory states are prepared to guarantee the limits of their actions, the continuation of the League of Nations' capacity, and the unanimous implementation of Article 19 of the League of Nations Covenant. In addition, France has formally guaranteed that it will not support any modifications based on previously agreed upon provisions. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

Rome: Experts drafting the final draft of the Four-Power Pact today deleted the third clause on disarmament and added new clauses stipulating the modification of the treaty, because the disarmament clauses will be negotiated separately based on the draft disarmament convention proposed by the British Prime Minister, so they were specially deleted. The section on modifying the treaty was advocated by Italy, Britain, and Germany, and after assurances to France that it would not affect the existing positions of the Little Entente and Poland, and that it would be handled entirely through the League of Nations, France agreed. It is now expected that the final draft can be drafted in Rome this afternoon. (National dispatch, 31st)

The Dispute Over the Definition of "Aggressor Nation"

France Advocates Natural Application of Sanctions

Britain Shrinks Back, Unwilling to Be Drawn into the Vortex

Seeking a Compromise Solution Again

(Geneva) The issue of defining an "aggressor nation," as a result of the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference's discussions over the past two days, has revealed significant differences of opinion. France and several other countries want a firm and unshakeable definition so that sanctions can be applied naturally in the event of aggression. Britain, on the other hand, wants a more flexible definition so as not to hinder independent judgment and action. Although the United States is not directly involved, it agrees with the British view. The draft resolution proposed by Greek representative Politis for the unreserved handling of this issue has been accepted by French representative Paul-Boncour. Chinese representative Wellington Koo also spoke in support, saying, "In our opinion, this case is a beneficial standard for determining who is the aggressor nation. Currently, there is no fixed provision regarding the definition of an aggressor nation, which leads to complex discussions and the inability to reach an agreement promptly. In cases of aggression, time is an important factor. An agreement on the definition of an aggressor nation would enhance the concept of security, as the aggressor nation would be deterred from acting. It is argued that listing aggressive acts may not be beneficial, as humans are cunning, especially countries that are more strategic. They will evade their actions and adjust their movements so that they can carry out acts of aggression in reality without being labeled as aggressors. If this is the case, a clear article on aggression will not promote international justice and the purpose of world peace, but will instead undermine it. However, according to the Chinese representative, deciding on an article on aggression, even if it is incomplete, is better than having no article at all. For this reason, the Chinese delegation supports the establishment of the second article of the draft concerning the definition of an aggressor nation." German and Hungarian representatives spoke against this draft. Finally, at the suggestion of Chairman Henderson, it was decided to hold a meeting, chaired by Greek representative Politis, with representatives from Britain and Russia, who hold completely opposing views, to seek a compromise solution. (Reuter's dispatch, 29th)

Disarmament Conference Discusses Banning Chemical Warfare

(Geneva) Today, the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference held only two meetings and completed the first reading of the three chapters of the British disarmament draft. These three chapters are (1) Proof of Aggressive Acts, (2) European Security Treaty, and (3) Prohibition of Chemical Warfare. The General Commission still intends to continue the meeting, but it was stopped by a declaration issued by French Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour. Paul-Boncour said that France will submit important amendments to the general provisions of the monitoring system and the disarmament convention tomorrow. It is reported that the amendments France intends to propose will advocate strengthening the restrictions on military expenditure budgets and the supervision of arms manufacturing. During today's discussion, representatives of several countries requested that the Security Treaty be applied to all countries in the world. US representative Davis pointed out that the meaning of prohibiting the use of force can be extended to the whole world, which is in line with the US view. French representative Paul-Boncour expressed France's unreserved support for the draft Security Convention, but said that the main point of the European Security Convention is to conclude a tighter agreement and add mutual assistance in addition to the prohibition of the use of force. The General Commission then discussed Chapter 4 of the British proposal, namely the chapter on the prohibition of chemical warfare. The spokesperson of the Little Entente, Titulescu, with the assistance of Paul-Boncour, argued that chemical warfare should be completely prohibited, without exception, and that retaliation should also be prohibited. If retaliation is necessary in the future, it should be limited to the joint sanctions stipulated in the Disarmament Convention. Chairman Henderson announced that the Presidium will set the agenda for the next few days tomorrow afternoon. Henderson's intention seems to be to ask the Disarmament Conference to continue the meeting, even if it extends to after the opening of the World Economic Conference on June 12, it will not be stopped. This matter was fiercely opposed by several delegations. Soviet Russian representative Litvinov has arrived here. (Havas dispatch, 30th)

The Puppet State Under Japanese Protection

Spit Upon by the Whole World

The League of Nations Plans to Forbid Its Participation in International Sports

Revised Report to Be Submitted for Discussion Next Week

(Geneva) The Secretariat of the League of Nations today issued the revised draft of the report prepared by the subcommittee on non-recognition of "Manchukuo." This revised draft summarizes and reiterates the original report, and adds one or two paragraphs, such as not allowing representatives of "Manchukuo" to participate in international sports events, such as the Davis Cup tennis tournament. The subcommittee is scheduled to meet on Thursday this week, and it is expected that this revised report will be submitted to the plenary meeting of the Advisory Committee next week. (Reuter's dispatch, 30th)

(Changchun) The "Manchukuo" authorities are eager to participate in the 1936 Olympic Games to be held in Berlin, but the first step is to have the Olympic Committee recognize "Manchukuo" as an independent country. "Manchu" Prime Minister Zheng Xiaoxu has entrusted Japanese representative Kana, who is attending the Olympic Conference, to find a way to do so. It is reported that the Japanese representative has promised to do his best to help. (Reuter's dispatch, 31st)

Lin and Dai Return to Nanjing Together

(Nanjing) Chairman Lin and President Dai's special train arrived in Nanjing at 11:00 am on the 30th. Niu Yongjian, Wang Yongbin, Lu Chao, Wei Huai, and hundreds of others greeted them at Pukou Station. After Lin and Dai crossed the river, they took a car back to the official residence to rest. (Central News Agency dispatch, 30th)

(Nanjing) Chairman Lin, President Dai, and his party went to Shaanxi at the beginning of the month to inspect the construction of the capital. They left Shaanxi a few days ago and returned to Nanjing. They inspected the Central Plains Cultural and Educational Center and various projects in the capital while passing through Luoyang. They also visited Langya Mountain and Zuiweng Pavilion in Chuzhou. They arrived in Nanjing at 11:00 am on the 30th by car from Chuzhou. A large number of people welcomed them at the station, and the police and military were also on guard at the station. Lin and Dai got off the car and crossed the river, and took a car to the official residence to rest. Chairman Lin told reporters that during this trip to Shaanxi, the disaster in the province was severe and should be relieved. Relief is divided into treating the symptoms and treating the root cause. Speaking of treating the symptoms, there are wailing everywhere in Shaanxi, and it is urgent to remit money for relief. It is also planned that the government will work with the Chinese and foreign charity associations to allocate funds to purchase seeds so that there is hope for the autumn harvest. To treat the root cause, the first priority is to build water conservancy projects. The Jingwei Canal project has been half completed and irrigates thousands of acres of farmland. If it is fully completed, the effect will be even greater. The Koukou Er River should also be dredged as soon as possible. In addition, it is planned to set up grain storage methods, divided into community granaries and official granaries. The second is to cultivate forests to regulate the climate. As for the construction of the capital, during the national crisis, we should strive to be thrifty. We are now surveying streets and developing transportation. The Longhai Railway has been laid to Weinan, and we hope that it will be open to Xi'an within the year. Dai said that the disaster in Shaanxi is very tragic. If relief is not given urgently, the victims will be everywhere and even become uninhabited. The Northwest Agricultural and Forestry College is now actively preparing for the school site, and it is planned to set up the Wugong Central Plains Cultural and Educational Center, which is also actively progressing. I have no other opinions on the current political situation other than hoping that the whole country will unite to overcome the difficulties. It is not yet decided whether I will go to Jiangxi to meet Chiang. (Central News Agency dispatch, 30th)

The Dalai Lama Cables the Military Affairs Commission

Denies Committing Offences in Kang

The Japanese Are Actually Thinking of Using the Panchen Lama

The New Provincial Committee of Anhui Takes Office

Liu Zhenhua Announces His Political Views on Governing Anhui

Wang Jun Arrives in Anqing to Meet with Liu

Japanese Troops Stationed in Beiping Conduct Street Fighting Exercises

Originally Intended to Visit the Observatory, but Were Dissuaded by Our Side

(Beiping) More than ninety guards from the Japanese Embassy stationed in Beiping set off from the Japanese barracks in Jiaomin Lane at around 9:00 am this morning, paraded in the area west of Guanyin Temple at Dongdan Archway, and conducted street fighting exercises at the old site of the Gongyuan. They did not return to the camp until noon. (Special dispatch, 31st)

Page 10

Current Commentary

Our Country Should Have Reservations About Disarmament Bao

Our Chinese representative declared at the Disarmament Conference, "Our country's coastline is long, and the territory adjacent to its territorial waters is constantly subject to armed invasion by the land, sea, and air forces of aggressor nations. Until the aggressive wars suffered by our country are finally resolved, we will not be subject to any restrictions... and reserve the right to resist aggression and protect our territory... It is regrettable that our belief in the peaceful settlement of international disputes has not been understood by the world." It is indeed regrettable, and it is also regrettable that our people have too much faith in peace and do not strive for their own strength to engage in self-defense of their territory and to protect their sovereignty.

The people of our country have always loved peace, and this historical tradition has a long history. From the late Qing Dynasty to the present, the facts are clear and need no further elaboration. Although the total number of soldiers in our country's army currently exceeds two million, transportation is difficult, and the territory covers an area of more than 34 million square miles. Our country is not like Japan, France, and other countries that use a conscription system. In addition to the standing army, there are also various reserves for military service that can be called upon. Moreover, modern scientific weapons are advancing day by day. Everything from airplanes in the air to tanks on land to long-distance train guns, which are being debated at the Geneva Disarmament Conference, can be used arbitrarily by the Japanese army to kill our people in the Northeast, while our country does not have this kind of equipment. Furthermore, in terms of naval strength, our country's navy is mostly composed of old ships from thirty years ago. Even if new ships are built, their size is very small, and the guns are limited to maintaining the safety of the ship's own navigation. At most, they are used to defend against pirate attacks and act as water police. It can be seen that there is absolutely no preparation for foreign warfare. Therefore, our country's reservation of the "right to protect territorial sovereignty and the right to resist aggression and self-defense" is the most fair and reasonable.

At the same time, while advocating disarmament in Geneva, the Japanese Army Department made a strange statement regarding military operations in North China, boasting that it could seize Beiping and Tianjin in the blink of an eye, and also proposed "If the responsible parties on the Chinese side are sincere in negotiations, the Japanese side will not hesitate to cooperate... but the Japanese army will remain stationed in the area, preparing for both "peace" and "war"... If the peace talks are unsuccessful due to the Chinese side's insincerity or if the war is provoked by inciting actions, the impact will be great. It is thought that the Chinese authorities will fully consider this." Alas, what is this saying? Since the September 18th Incident, who is ultimately responsible for inciting the conflict? There is no need for our people to argue. Even Lord Lytton, a decades-old friend of Japan, has clearly stated this. Uchida's "scorched earth diplomacy" also explained its military policy in another aspect. Therefore, the Japanese so-called "sincerity" is nothing other than that pointed at the tip of the military's spear. In this era when military power is almighty and reason is obliterated, militarists can arbitrarily act rampantly, disregard credibility, and have no regard for anything. However, the subsequent disputes are still unpredictable. For the sake of our country's future and for the sake of world peace, the first thing we must know is that the outcome of international disputes is not like the relationship between personal interests and rewards that can be determined in an instant. It must rely on a considerable period of hard struggle and effort to reverse the decline and save ourselves. Second, we should not be discouraged by the current setbacks. We must know that "three households can destroy Qin / one turn can restore the dynasty." Moreover, although our country is becoming weaker day by day, there are many opportunities for revival. It depends on how hard our people work.

In short, the reduction of armaments is something we wholeheartedly support. However, it is necessary for aggressors to fully reflect on themselves, and for the friendly nations participating in disarmament to be able to actually sanction those who rely solely on military force as a tool of aggression. Then our country should do its best to uphold peace. Otherwise, it is better to reserve the right to self-defense and protect our territory in order to plan for the future of self-rescue.

The Middle East Railway Problem is Serious, Pseudo-Implements Blockade of Suifenhe Station

Russian Gunboats Fire on Pseudo-Manchu Vessels

The Pseudo-Regime Actually Changed the Name of the East Railway

(Harbin) Sato, the railway officer of the (pseudo) Manchukuo Railway Department, forcibly sealed off the Suifenhe Station on the Russian-Manchu border at 6:00 am this morning. (Dentsu dispatch, 31st)

(Changchun) The Soviet Russian authorities' detention of cargo trains on the Middle East Railway has not stopped to this day. The (pseudo) Manchukuo Ministry of Transportation is very angry and has decided to cut off the Russian-Manchu connection line in Suifenhe. This blockade will be implemented at 2:00 pm on the 31st. The Ministry of Transportation issued a statement today, saying that Soviet Russia continues to detain cargo trains on the Middle East Railway and transport them into Russian territory. Although the "Manchukuo" has repeatedly warned them, they have not stopped their actions. This attitude of Soviet Russia violates the agreement and is an illegal act of abandoning the Middle East Railway Ussuri connection agreement. "Manchukuo" cannot tolerate this illegal act in the position of jointly operating the Middle East Railway. The Russian-Manchu connection point is now cut off in order to seek the reflection of Soviet Russia. (Japan Allied News dispatch, 30th)

(Harbin) According to news from the Manchukuo Ministry of Transportation in Changchun, from June 1, the Middle East Railway will be renamed the "North Manchuria Railway." This is the second discussion by the Ministry of Transportation on the renaming event. The Ministry will immediately notify the Russian Director of the Middle East Railway of the renaming. (Reuter's dispatch, 31st)

(Harbin) Soviet warships near Tongjiang detained "Manchukuo" ships. The Magistrate of Tongjiang County reported to the authorities here on the 28th, stating (1) that there were several Soviet Russian gunboats patrolling at the intersection of the Songhua River and Heilongjiang River, and (2) that ships traveling between Tongjiang and Boli were fired on or detained by Soviet Russian gunboats. Therefore, the residents of the upstream area lack food and are very poor. (Japan Allied News dispatch, 30th)

If Japan Protests the New Tariff Rates

Our Side Decides to Refute

(Nanjing) Foreign news reports that the Japanese government has decided to protest our newly promulgated import tax. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not yet received the protest letter. According to an official, the Sino-Japanese tariff agreement expired on May 16. Our country has the autonomous right to collect customs duties, and Japan has no right to interfere. Moreover, the tax rate levied by our country on Japanese goods is completely equal to the tax rate levied on goods from other countries. The Japanese government's protest is obviously unreasonable. Furthermore, our country's increase in tax rates is entirely based on the fundamental principle of economic hardship. Since the September 18th Incident, the Japanese army has occupied our four provincial territories, gradually and completely plundering the customs, salt, and postal rights of each province, causing great impact on our country's financial income. However, our payment of foreign debts, such as the Boxer Indemnity, has not been delayed or shortened as a result. Our country has increased tax rates in order to relieve financial difficulties, and this is an unavoidable hardship that should not be interfered with by other countries. Therefore, if Japan protests to us, it will be refuted. (Central News Agency dispatch, 31st)

Chinese and Foreign Warships Stationed in Hankou for Investigation

(Hankou) The Japanese 24th Destroyer Fleet, including the Taoyuu and other four ships, returned to Hankou from Yichang on the 30th. Together with the An Zhai and others, there are a total of nine ships stationed. In addition, there are six British ships, one American ship, two French and Italian ships, and eleven Chinese ships, for a total of thirty-one ships stationed in Hankou. Opening of the Economic Conference

Roosevelt's Instructions to the Delegation

Strive for Currency Stability

And Hope to Stop International Trade Wars

War Debt Issue to be Discussed Outside the Conference

Japan Opposes Moving the Conference to Geneva

(Washington) The US delegation to the World Economic Conference is about to depart for England. President Roosevelt has compiled a series of instructions. According to these instructions, the US delegation should strive for currency stabilization and tariff reduction simultaneously. The US government believes that these two issues are closely related. If currency is stabilized without stopping trade wars, currency stabilization cannot be sustained. Conversely, if currency remains chaotic, signing trade agreements is meaningless. Regarding currency issues, the US delegation should strive to increase the price of silver and adopt a gold and silver bimetallic standard. The White House has stated that news reports regarding Roosevelt's solution to war debts are "purely speculative." Roosevelt does not intend to request full authority from Congress on this matter but plans to take responsibility and resolve it during the congressional recess, seeking congressional ratification afterward. Roosevelt intends to provide significant convenience to debtor nations regarding the war debts due on June 15, the day the World Economic Conference closes on June 12, to alleviate various difficulties. (31st Havas dispatch)

(Washington) Today, US President Roosevelt denied reports that he intended to use the treaty-making powers granted by Congress to resolve the war debt issue. Congress had authorized the President to negotiate reciprocal trade agreements and adjust tariffs. Recently, newspapers have speculated that Roosevelt would also address the war debt issue when negotiating trade agreements, allowing countries to reduce principal and pay a portion of overdue debts. The White House denied this today, stating that it was purely speculative and that the President has no intention of using this power to modify the war debt. Moreover, apart from negotiating reciprocal trade agreements, all of the President's treaty-making powers are shared with the Senate, which has not yet taken any measures to modify the war debt repayment schedule. Therefore, the war debt issue, under the current circumstances, seems likely to be discussed outside the London Economic Conference, with various proposals and the President's recommendations submitted to Congress for independent decision-making. (30th National News dispatch)

(Tokyo) The League of Nations Secretariat proposed that the World Economic Conference be moved to Geneva to be held simultaneously with the Disarmament Conference. Japan currently opposes this proposal. Political circles claim that the convocation of the World Economic Conference is to achieve economic relief and has nothing to do with the Disarmament Conference. (30th Reuters dispatch)

Song Ziwen Departs US for England

(New York) Song Ziwen, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance of China, and a delegate to the World Economic Conference, set off for London tonight. The Chinese delegation includes a total of eleven people, including Sir Robert Ho Tung. (31st Havas dispatch)

US Delegation Prepares to Depart

(Washington) President Roosevelt has appointed Morrison, a banker from San Antonio, Texas, as the sixth US delegate to the World Economic Conference. The entire delegation is scheduled to depart for London tonight. The confirmed composition is as follows: Secretary of State Hull, former Democratic presidential candidate Cox, Chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee Pittman, Chairman of the House Foreign Affairs Committee McReynolds, Republican Senator Johnson of Michigan, and the sixth person, Morrison. The delegation's specialists are State Department Assistant Berle, legal advisor Nelson, and economic advisor Feis. There are also fifteen other technical advisors. According to the President, the remaining personnel have not yet been determined. (30th Havas dispatch)

Speeches Limited to Ten Minutes

(Washington) Senator Pittman stated today that he will propose that each country's delegation be limited to ten minutes of speaking time at the opening of the World Economic Conference. (29th Reuters dispatch)

US Instructions Support Bimetallism

(Washington) The House Foreign Affairs Committee voted today to instruct the US delegation attending the World Economic Conference to support bimetallism based on a fixed ratio between gold and silver. (30th Reuters dispatch)

Swiss Delegation Determined

Bear City The members of the Swiss delegation to the World Economic Conference have been decided, and President Schulthess will lead them to London. (30th Havas dispatch)

Ishii's Radio Address

Pleads Friendship, Seeks US Understanding

Indulges in Arbitrary Attacks on China and Russia

(New York) Ishii, the Japanese delegate to the World Economic Conference, gave a radio address here tonight, praising President Roosevelt as astute and compassionate, resolute and fair, and continuing the traditional friendship between Japan and the United States, unchanged by recent events. He continued to describe the special difficulties in dealing with the situation in the Far East, stating that the forces of corruption and chaos are gradually encroaching upon a region of utmost importance to us, affecting our survival. We must resist them, and we must know that this region is adjacent to a large country whose aim is to destroy all the creeds, organizations, and institutions that you, we, and most of the civilized world deem necessary or even sacred. We must also know that this region is adjacent to another large country where turmoil is the norm, illegality is law, and bad governance is governance. Unfortunately, we are neighbors with these two great powers, and Heaven knows the difficulties of dealing with them. We will continue to deal with them, but the difficulties and incidents are endless. (29th Reuters dispatch)

U.S. House Passes Bill Abolishing Gold Standard

Treasury Secretary Woodin Indicates He Will Remain in Office Temporarily

Washington, 29th (National Telegram). The U.S. Gold Standard Act is expected to be completely abolished before the end of this week. The House of Representatives passed the abolition bill today, and the Senate is also expected to pass it within the next day or two. Once the Gold Standard Act is abolished, the U.S. President can set the price of gold at any time without fear of anyone bringing it to the Supreme Court. According to the final report of the House Banking and Currency Committee, this bill only legalizes the emergency power given to the U.S. President and is not in itself a means of inflating currency. It also stated that abolishing the Gold Standard Act is tantamount to declaring that fulfilling the gold clauses in bonds is contrary to the public interest. Today, the Republican Party argued during the debate that this procedure was unconstitutional, but the Democratic Party responded that the Constitution authorizes Congress to issue currency and set its value, but does not prohibit delegating this power to executive agencies. It is expected that this bill will immediately absorb gold coins hidden by the public, as the value of these gold coins can no longer be higher than any legal currency. As for the composition of gold coins, it will remain the same for the time being, but it may be changed in the future after the President consults with foreign politicians.

Washington, 29th (National Telegram). Friends of U.S. Treasury Secretary Woodin stated today that Woodin does not want to resign during this turbulent period, but will resign from the cabinet after the turbulence subsides. As for his purchase of securities from Morgan Silver Company at a low price and resale in the market for profit before becoming Treasury Secretary, it was not an illegal act, and everyone in the country wants to do it.

U.S. and Russia Exchange Products

Negotiations to Begin Soon

New York, 30th (Reuters). It is reported that the U.S. government will soon begin negotiations with Soviet Russian representatives on the exchange of products. The main U.S. products will be cotton and livestock, while the Soviet Russian products will be manganese, chromium, pulp, and asbestos. Former Senator Brookhart has recently been appointed as a special assistant to the Department of Agriculture to study the possibility of exporting U.S. products to Eastern Europe. According to Brookhart, he will closely monitor trade between the U.S. and Russia. In 1932, the volume of trade between the two countries was only one-tenth of the previous year.

Gandhi's Fast Breaks Class Discrimination

Famous Temples Open to Untouchables

Nairobi, East Africa, 29th (Reuters). Today, an Indian temple here allowed untouchables to enter, which is unprecedented in East African history. The doors of the temple were locked by the custodian, but today they were opened to allow a woman from a higher-class Indian family to enter. Then, a large team organized by the Arya Gandhi Association arrived at the temple, including many untouchable men and women, all of whom were invited to enter the temple. Most of the custodians agreed with this unprecedented move, but a few still opposed it. After the untouchables entered the temple, they did not express anything and remained orderly. In addition, an Indian organization held a tea party, where several Indian leaders entertained some untouchables. All of this was moved by Gandhi's fast.

Poona, 30th (Reuters). Gandhi's 21-day fast ended yesterday. Although he is very weak, he was very pleased to receive a telegram today stating that the famous Shiva temple in Rishikesh, India, has now been opened to untouchables. Although Gandhi's fast has ended, he is not yet out of danger and can only take some nourishing substances such as fruit juice and honey water. It is estimated that he will not be able to eat other foods for the next ten days. Doctors examined Gandhi today and forbade him from participating in politics and reading letters.

Persian Parliament Approves Anglo-Persian Oil Agreement

Tehran, 30th (Reuters). The Persian Parliament today approved the Anglo-Persian oil agreement. It will take effect after the Persian King signs it. The new agreement allows the oil company to explore oil fields in southwestern Persia, with the area reduced by about half compared to the original. It also stipulates that the company must abandon any parts of the area that it fails to explore by 1938, with the total area not exceeding 100,000 square miles. According to this agreement, the company does not have the exclusive right to install oil pipelines. In addition to paying a tax of four shillings per ton, the company should pay one-fifth of its net profit to the Persian government. If the British exchange rate falls, the company must compensate for the exchange losses. This concession is valid for sixty years, after which Persia can recover all of the company's assets. The company agrees to hire as many Persians as possible and to pay 100,000 pounds of British gold annually for the expenses of Persian students studying engineering in the UK. If the company is willing to liquidate or fails to comply with the provisions of this agreement, the Persian government has the right to cancel this concession, but such cancellation must be notified two years in advance.

Diplomatic Dispute: Austria Retaliates Against Germany

Vienna, 30th (Havas). The Austrian government's cold shoulder to German cabinet members visiting Austria has caused a diplomatic dispute between the two countries. Germany has taken retaliatory measures in response, requiring Germans who want to travel to Austria to pay a passport fee of 1,000 marks, as a way of imposing a prohibition through taxation. This law has been announced and will take effect on June 1st. Various Austrian ministries have jointly formed an economic committee to study countermeasures. This afternoon, the committee drafted various proposals, such as (1) Austrians traveling to Germany must have passports, (2) Restrictions will be placed on German imports to make their quantity equal to Austrian exports to Germany.

Japanese Reporter Explores the Mystery of the Volcano Bottom

Tokyo, 30th (Japan United Press). The recent suicides at Mount Mihara on Izu Oshima have caused people to have a mysterious sense of terror. The Tokyo Yomiuri Shimbun has decided to explore the mystery of the bottom of the crater and has been making concrete preparations since the end of April. On the 4th, animals such as monkeys and rabbits were lowered into the crater to conduct animal experiments. The results proved that the human body could be lowered to 1,000 feet. Therefore, the deputy chief of the social department, Iwata Tokunosuke, the photography department chief, Magara Toku, and Westerners formed an expedition team and stayed near Mount Mihara to study the weather every day. On the 29th, all preparations were completed, and this unprecedented adventure was carried out at 2:30 p.m. The wind speed was 7 meters per second that day, and the weather was quite clear. Department Chief Iwata entered the crater and descended to a position of 1,250 feet, where he discovered a dead body of a suicide victim. After inspecting the tragic eruption situation inside the crater, he came out safely. Next, Photography Department Chief Magara descended and photographed many desolate scenes.

Wang, Sun, Luo, Huang, and Others Arrive in Lushan One After Another to Meet Chiang

Concrete Decisions Made on Domestic and Foreign Policies

Jiujiang Communication. Since Huang Fu arrived in Ping, a truce atmosphere has permeated the country. The authorities believe that this matter is of great importance and must be handled with caution. Another communication. After returning to Nanjing from Beiping, Interior Minister Huang Shaoxiong flew from Nanjing to Jiangxi by plane at 10:00 a.m. on the 29th. Before Huang came to Jiangxi, he received news that Wang, Sun, and Chiang were going to meet in Lushan. Therefore, when he flew to Jiujiang, he originally planned to land at the Xun airport. However, due to the deep accumulation of water at the airport, there was a risk of danger when landing. So, he drove directly to Nanchang and landed safely at the airport outside Shunhua Gate at 1:35 p.m. Few people knew about it beforehand, so there were not many welcomers. Only the headquarters received a phone call and sent people to take care of everything at the airport. After getting off the plane, Huang immediately took a car prepared by the headquarters and rushed to the ferry, took the Naxun Road transport across the river, and transferred to a Naxun Road special car to Xun to rush to Lushan, arriving at around 6:00 p.m. He immediately met with Presidents Wang and Sun and Chairman Chiang to report on the situation in North China and the recent military actions of the Japanese and puppet forces. Decision on Representatives for Sino-Japanese Ceasefire Negotiations

Our Main Personnel are Xiong Bin

Location Decided at China Merchants Bureau in Tanggu

Difficult Issues Still in Negotiation

Special Dispatch from Beiping. Since the four principles were agreed upon on the morning of the 23rd, both sides have begun to proceed accordingly. The first step is to implement an actual ceasefire. Both sides sent representatives to the agreed location to discuss in detail the provisional defense areas of the two armies and all ceasefire procedures. On the 25th, it was completely completed. The representatives of both sides expressed their satisfaction in an oral form, shook hands with each other, and the ceremony was completed. After this step was completed, the troops of both sides withdrew to the appropriate locations and implemented the ceasefire. In recent days, more in-depth negotiations have been underway, and everything is going smoothly. Yesterday (28th), there was an important meeting in Ju Ren Tang. Except for Yu Xuezhong, who was unable to arrive due to busy government affairs, Song Zheyuan, Shang Zhen, Pang Bingxun, Fu Zuoyi, Wan Fulin, Zhang Qun, Jiang Bocheng, and others all attended. Huang Fu personally discussed with everyone and generally reached a conclusion. Military affairs are still emphasized in dealing with Japan. The first step is to resolve the war issue, and diplomacy and politics will not be involved for the time being. Within the next few days, military personnel from Japan will jointly discuss ceasefire steps. The Japanese side initially suggested that the negotiation location be in Qinhuangdao, while the Chinese side considered Tanggu to be appropriate. After several consultations, the Japanese side finally agreed, and the meeting place was decided to be at the Tanggu China Merchants Bureau. Both sides have each appointed six representatives. It is said that the main personnel on our side is Mr. Xiong Bin, and the Japanese side is Mr. Okamura. Both are military personnel. Okamura is currently serving in the Army Headquarters, participating in military affairs, and is Koiso's deputy. Regarding the ceasefire measures, he will be based on Mutō's orders. The cessation of hostilities will inevitably involve detailed discussions. Japanese Ambassador Arima will arrive in Ping from Shanghai within the next few days, but will not attend the meeting. He is only an advisor, and his mission is only to report everything to the Japanese government.

Today (29th), Huang, He, and military and political leaders such as Jiang Bocheng and Zhang Qun held another meeting in Fengze Garden to discuss all issues in more detail. There are many difficulties in these peace negotiations: (1) The Japanese side has never forgotten the recognition of Manchuria and directly demands that our country recognize it, which is difficult to do. It is feared that they will use roundabout methods to reveal this intention and may ask to add the words "Japanese troops withdraw to the Manchurian border" in the withdrawal text in the future. If we do not pay attention and rashly sign, it will be tantamount to disguised recognition of Manchuria. (2) Even if the "Manchurian State" is not specified in the withdrawal text, if the Japanese and Manchurian armies are used together, it will be tantamount to disguised demand for recognition of Manchuria. (3) Since the Japanese army invaded the mainland on a large scale, it has bought a large number of traitors and organized puppet troops to make trouble in the mainland. The aftermath of these puppet troops is very difficult. (4) In order to ensure the safety of their military occupation areas, the Japanese side has made extravagant demands on the scope of the demilitarized zone. All of these are extremely difficult issues in the peace negotiations and require careful consideration. The front-line war has subsided since the 24th. Tongzhou and Shunyi have each withdrawn several miles to avoid conflicts. Although the puppet army in eastern Tianjin is still active, it is not very strong. Today, the front line is very peaceful. The Japanese army in Tongzhou is still stationed in the areas of Xixia and Yanxiao, more than 30 miles away from Tongzhou County. Most of our army is west of Tongzhou, and only a small number of troops are stationed in the city, confronting each other. In Shunyi, the Japanese army is stationed north of Niulanshan, and our army is defending Shunyi and both sides, without any movement. In Lutai, the Japanese army is in the Yangshizhuang area, and the Japanese army east of the Ninghe River is in the Miaojiazhuang area. Our army is still stationed in its original position. As for the plainclothes team found north of Langfang and Luobao, it is the disruptive behavior of the puppet army and has nothing to do with the overall situation.

The internal organization of the Executive Yuan's Beiping Political Affairs Consolidation Committee has been completed. It was originally scheduled to be formally established on June 1st, but because the time is too short and the preparations are insufficient, it is expected to be established before June 10th. Huang Shaoxiong rushed to Nanjing the day before yesterday to visit Wang, Luo, and others to report on the recent situation in North China. When he arrived in Nanjing, he learned that Wang and others had already gone to Jiangxi. Huang also went to Jiangxi to participate in the meeting. It is expected that the opening day of the Political Affairs Consolidation Committee will be after Huang returns north. As for the important generals in North China, they will also attend the routine meeting of the Military Affairs Branch on Wednesday this week to discuss military matters. The Japanese planes did not arrive in Beiping today (29th). The Japanese aircraft carrier Notoro, which was anchored outside Dagukou, set sail on the evening of the 27th. (May 29th)

Wedding Guests Mishandle Gun, Causing Disaster

Editor of the People's Daily Acquitted

The case of the construction of a monument to the general manager in Ximen Yuecheng has caused disputes among local people. After the provincial government decided to move the monument to Zhongshan Park, the original monument construction site in Ximen Yuecheng was reserved for future public construction, and the county was ordered to preserve it and announce it. Later, Wu Boyang built a fence there. The People's Daily, organized by the local county party headquarters, accused him of disobeying orders and acting like a local bully. After the county government ordered the Public Security Bureau to strictly limit Wu's removal, Wu believed that Yang Yunwen, the editor of the People's Daily, defamed his reputation and filed a lawsuit in the county court, requesting legal action and attaching a private lawsuit to compensate for the loss of reputation. This afternoon (31st) at 2:00 p.m., Judge Zhang Yihuang of the court summoned both parties for interrogation. Regarding the point of the local bully in the article, it was said that the plaintiff knew the provincial order and still built a fence, disobeying the order, which was beyond doubt. After the county ordered its removal, it can be seen that the construction of the fence was illegal. The plaintiff's lawsuit is groundless, etc. Both parties argued vigorously and endlessly. After the interrogator ordered the debate to end, he declared Ye Dingchu and Yang Yunwen not guilty and withdrew.

Suzhou

Two Shops in Huguan Town Robbed

The Yao Qiantai bean curd shop and Ruiyuan soy sauce workshop in Xiatang North Street, Huguanshu Town, were robbed at about 9:00 p.m. on the 30th by eight or nine robbers wearing gray short coats, each holding box guns and pistols. Wuxi

Joint Conference of the Silk Cocoon Industry

Tan Xihong, the Director of the Land Reclamation Department of the Ministry of Industry, believes that Wuxi is the richest cocoon-producing area in Jiangsu Province. Now that new cocoons are on the market, at a time when the rural economy is extremely depressed and silk cocoons have failed for years, it is necessary to conduct inspections and investigations. He specially invited Dong Xiujia, the Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department, to come to Wuxi at 1:00 p.m. on the 30th. He telegraphed the two silk cocoon trade associations in advance to convene the industry to hold a joint conference to consult on matters. After Director Tan and Director Dong arrived in Wuxi, they first had a conversation with County Chief Yan Zuoyi and then participated in the silk cocoon industry conference. More than 40 industry leaders attended that day. Chairman Hua Shaochun first reported the reasons for the failure of silk cocoons in Wuxi, which was the opening of cocoon shops. There are now 368 cocoon shops in Wuxi County that have joined the association, and there are also more than 100 that have not joined the association, totaling more than 500. However, there is not much silk cocoon production, so the supply and demand cannot correspond, which has led to difficulties for both farmers and merchants. The opening of the new cocoon market was decided by this conference to be on June 1st. Unexpectedly, a few merchants, under the pretext of testing the reeling yield, took the liberty of starting earlier, having already opened the market three days ago. As for the cocoon price, according to the original plan decided by the Silk Industry Unified Committee, it was agreed to be 35 yuan for improved varieties and 25 yuan for local varieties based on the European and American silk markets. Now, it has been repeatedly reported that some shops that have opened the market have released prices of up to 45 and 50 yuan. Such destruction of the agreed rules is obviously intentional disruption and should be discussed at length, and the government should punish those who disrupt the overall situation as a warning to others. After Director Tan, Director Dong, and the two county chiefs expressed their opinions successively, and the silk cocoon industry had detailed consultations, the results of the discussions were as follows: (A) Cocoon price issue: (1) Because the weather in Wuxi is good and the reeling yield is shorter, the highest price for improved varieties of new cocoons is approved to be 40 yuan. (2) If there is any release of prices or scales, once verified, a request will be made to the government to immediately revoke the shop license, and all losses of the shop owner will be borne by the operating merchants. (B) Opening date: (1) According to the conference decision, it will be June 1st. No opening will be allowed on the 31st. The industry attending the meeting today will be responsible for complying with this and request the County Government Public Security Bureau to telegraph each branch to strictly investigate. If anyone opens the market without authorization, they will be ordered to stop. Those who do not comply will have their cocoon scales reported to the County Bureau for punishment. (2) If the industry discovers that neighboring shops are opening the market ahead of schedule, they can only advise them to stop and cannot blindly follow. If they do not comply, they will report to the association and forward the report to the County Government for punishment.

Changzhou

Cocoon Industry Association Holds General Meeting

The Wuyi Cocoon Industry Association, with the upcoming fresh cocoon season, specifically convened a general meeting of all members at approximately 1:00 PM on the 29th. Forty-five cocoon trading firms reported their presence. The meeting was chaired by Zhao Songping, and the following matters were discussed: (1) It was resolved that each cocoon trading firm should first register with the Business Tax Bureau, obtain a certificate for verification, and simultaneously register with the association for record-keeping and future coordination. (2) It was resolved that each firm should purchase and use stamp tax independently from the Stamp Tax Bureau. (3) It was resolved that the opening date for purchasing would be June 1st. (4) It was resolved that the price of cocoons would be set at thirty-five to forty yuan per dan (unit of weight) for improved varieties and twenty-five to thirty yuan per dan for local varieties.

Robbery Occurs in Suburban Area

At approximately 10:00 PM on the 28th, a group of armed bandits suddenly raided the residence of Bai Kun, located at Baijia Bridge, Xiatang, east of Wuyi city. They wantonly ransacked the house for about an hour before leaving. It is reported that dozens of articles of clothing and ornaments were lost. The location is very close to the city, and the incident has caused panic among nearby residents.

Notorious Thieves Apprehended in the Fifteenth District

Zhou Daonan, an assistant officer in the Fifteenth District of Wuyi, learned on the 29th that bandits were hiding near Lüshi Bridge. He led district guards and the local defense corps to the area. Zhou moved ahead and encountered the notorious bandit Yang Zhengda near Benniu. He immediately seized Yang and brought him to the district office. Under interrogation by District Chief Zhang Renhe, Yang confessed to several crimes and implicated accomplices, including Li Jinsheng. Subsequently, Li Jinsheng was also captured. He admitted to participating in robberies of boats at Sanli'an and Yangqiao, among other places. The two criminals were handed over to the county authorities on the 31st for interrogation and legal proceedings.

Nantong

Verdict in Water Police Officer Extortion Case

Chen Yide, the head of the investigation team of the Fourth District Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police stationed in Tongzhou, was found guilty of unlawfully detaining Liu, a farmer, and Chen Mingdao, a farmer, inside a patrol boat cabin at Rengang and extorting a large sum of money. The case was uncovered by the Public Security Bureau and transferred to the court. Chen Yide denied kidnapping but admitted to deficiencies in the handling of the case. After the criminal court concluded its inquiry and delivered its verdict, Chen Yide was fined five hundred yuan for extortion, with a penalty of imprisonment at a rate of two yuan per day in lieu of payment.

Preliminary Election Representatives Chosen in All Districts

In Nantong's preliminary elections for representatives to the National Provisional Representative Assembly, the Provincial Committee member Xia Dingwen came to Nantong to oversee the process. The results of the ballot count showed that Chen Guanying, Wu Jianzhang, and Li Zemao were elected.

Hangzhou

Murder Case at Zhendong Building

Song Baofu, a 28-year-old resident of No. 44 Zhendong Building in Hangzhou, originally from Shaoxing. His wife, Li, was only nineteen years old. Song himself was serving as a captain in the Fenghua Defense Corps. His wife lived with her mother, Li Xu. Lü Guanzhe, a 35-year-old man from Sheng County and a close friend of Song, was an official in the surveying team of the Department of Civil Affairs. Since Song was not often at home, Lü frequently visited under the guise of checking in. He engaged in an affair with Li, which had lasted for over a year. Recently, Lü heard rumors that Song's wife had formed a new relationship. Consumed by jealousy, he went to Song's house on the evening of the 30th to spend the night. At around 5:00 AM yesterday (the 31st), he secretly took a kitchen knife from the kitchen and, while Song's wife was fast asleep, struck her head with a fierce blow. The woman, in extreme pain, woke up and cried out as she tried to escape. Lü then wildly slashed at her head, arms, hands, and chest more than a dozen times. The woman immediately collapsed in a pool of blood. Neighbors heard the commotion and promptly reported it to the police station. Police officers rushed to the scene. The perpetrator, realizing that he could not escape the law, repeatedly struck his own head with the kitchen knife, causing blood to flow profusely. Patrol Officer Zhou Chunshou urgently sent the injured to the nearby Gulou Hospital for treatment. Doctors stated that Song's wife was in critical condition due to severe injuries and excessive blood loss. Lü's injuries were relatively minor. Ke Shiming, an officer from the Second Division of the First District, briefly questioned Lü, who confessed to the crime of passion. He was then transferred to the Hangzhou District Court for legal proceedings.

Suicide by Drowning After Prolonged Illness

Zhu Yutang, a shop assistant at the former Xinkang Shoe Store in Hangzhou, suffered from typhoid fever for a long time without recovery. With a poor family background, he became despondent about his life. On the afternoon of the 30th, at 1:00 PM, he secretly threw himself into a well. He was discovered and rescued, still showing faint signs of life. He was immediately sent to the hospital for treatment, but it was too late to revive him. The store manager, Yun Duansheng, provided a coffin and prepared the body for burial.

Ningbo

Intense Battle Between Water Police and Pirates

After the Taizhou merchant vessel, which sailed between Shanghai and Taiwan, was robbed by bandits in the Bai Sha Yang waters off the coast of Taiwan, the water police team stationed there, led by Patrol Officers Jin Xieguang and He Zhen, along with Qiu Shirong, platoon leader of the Jinqing Port Security Team, set out to suppress the pirates. On the 26th of this month, at around 3:00 PM, they encountered the pirates east of Jinmao Port. A fierce exchange of fire ensued, lasting until 3:00 AM on the 27th, when the bandits finally lost ground and fled in disarray. Four pirates were killed on the spot, and one wounded pirate, Lin Erdi, was captured. The police also seized three quick-firing rifles, one Mauser rifle, one carbine, and one wooden-holster pistol. Two water police officers, Huang Zhengqi and Li Chang'an, were killed by gunfire, and one, Tao Jinhuai, was wounded. Lin Erdi confessed to participating in the robbery of the Taizhou vessel. He has now been transferred to the Water Police Bureau for investigation and further legal action.

Local News

On the Different Views Regarding the Ceasefire in North China

City Chamber of Commerce Sends Telegram of Advice

Central Government and Provinces Should Prepare for a Last Stand

Do Not Engage in Empty Accusations and Mutual Blame

In response to the recent debates regarding the ceasefire in North China, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent a special telegram of advice. The telegram reads: "To the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Military Affairs Commission, the Guangzhou Southwest Political Committee, the Peiping Military Affairs Commission Branch, the Fuzhou Fujian Provincial Government, Mr. Hu Zhantang in Hong Kong, and Mr. Feng Huanzhang in Chahar. Recent discussions regarding the ceasefire in North China have sparked varying viewpoints, leading to widespread rumors and anxieties, creating a 'boiling beans' scenario where people are uncertain and fearful. Our country boasts a military force of over two million, with only about twenty divisions tied down by military engagements in Jiangxi Province. If all parties can prioritize the overall situation and promptly send reinforcements north, how could the battles at the various passes of the Great Wall have resulted in such a disadvantageous situation, surrendering thousands of miles east of the Liao River to the enemy? The current ceasefire issue stems from this situation. Both the front lines and the rear guard should bear their respective responsibilities. At this time, the Central Government and various provinces should earnestly prepare for a last stand should negotiations fail. Empty accusations and mutual blame should be avoided. During the late Ming Dynasty, with the Qing army poised to cross the river, Zuo Liangyu was still raising troops in the upper reaches, leading to internal strife and the eventual collapse of the dynasty. This historical lesson is a clear warning for today. To repeat this would leave the people with nowhere to die. We respectfully offer this advice, hoping for your consideration. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce bows in respect."

The Shanghai University Students' Federation telegraphed Huang Fu yesterday, stating that negotiations must not involve politics. Commemoration of the May 30th Incident Held the Day Before Yesterday

City Party Headquarters Convened a Commemorative Meeting

At 10:00 AM on the 30th, the Shanghai City Party Headquarters convened a commemorative meeting for the eighth anniversary of the May 30th Massacre in the auditorium on the third floor of the City Party Headquarters. Executive Committee member Lu Jingshi presided over the meeting. The Second District Police Station dispatched a team of police officers to provide security at the venue. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 AM.

Commemorative Ceremony

(1) All stood in solemn silence. (2) The Party anthem was sung. (3) The national flag and the portrait of the Founding Father were saluted with the highest respect. (4) The chairman reverently recited the Founding Father's last will and testament. (5) Three minutes of silence were observed to commemorate the martyrs of the May 30th Incident. (6) The chairman gave a report. (7) Speeches were delivered. (8) Slogans were chanted. (9) The ceremony concluded.

Participating Representatives: Li Zemin from the City Public Security Bureau, Zhang Menglin from the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Ma Jiazhen from the City Education Association, Jiang Zongjian from the Jianghai Customs Superintendent Office, Lu Bolian from the Shanghai Branch of National Medicine, Zhu Xuefan from the General Labor Union, Zhang Huichun from the Shanghai South District Farmers' Association, and over three hundred people from various schools, Party branches at all levels, and people's organizations.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Lu Jingshi reported, in brief, that the remote cause of the May 30th Massacre was China's subjugation to unequal treaties. Its immediate cause was the unprecedented oppression of the Chinese people by the collusion of imperialists. However, although the May 30th Incident resulted in the sacrifice of many people, the internal strife among warlords prevented it from achieving victory. This infighting was backed by imperialism, which relied on unequal treaties to encourage this internal strife. Therefore, to escape the oppression of imperialism, we must unite to abolish unequal treaties, etc.

Commemorative Slogans

(1) The spirit of the May 30th martyrs will never die! (2) Down with Japanese imperialism!

(3) Eliminate the Chinese Communist Party! (4) Long live the Chinese Nationalist Party! (5) Long live the Republic of China!

Naming Ceremony for Shanghai City's First Airplane Held Today

Ministry of Military Affairs Dispatches Ge Jingen to Shanghai to Receive It

American Major Doolittle and Others to Perform

The China Aviation Association ordered eighteen Hawk fighter planes from the United States. One plane has already arrived and will be named "Shanghai City" today. The naming ceremony will be held at 2:00 PM today at the Jiangwan Racecourse, after which it will be donated to the government. A telegram was sent to Chiang Kai-shek, the chairman of the Military Affairs Commission of the Aviation Administration of the Ministry of Military Affairs, requesting that he send representatives to attend the ceremony. The Ministry of Military Affairs has dispatched Ge Jingen, the director of the Aviation Administration, to Shanghai today by plane to receive the aircraft. American Major Doolittle, Louis, Dwen Sun, Kong Wu and others will perform various stunts. Details are as follows:

(2) Urgent, To Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission of the Military Affairs Ministry in Nanjing and Nanchang: Our association has scheduled the naming ceremony for the "Shanghai City" airplane for 2:00 PM on June 1st at the Jiangwan Racecourse. Regards, Military Affairs Ministry, Director Ge Jingen of the Aviation Administration." The Aviation Association also telegraphed Mao Bangchu, the principal of the Central Aviation School, requesting that he come to Shanghai to participate. Mr. Mao may also be arriving with Director Ge.

Venue Arrangement

The venue is set at the Jiangwan Racecourse. The venue is decorated with flags of various nations. Our national flag is raised at the highest point. A platform is set up at the main entrance of the racetrack, displaying the Party and national flags and the portrait of the Founding Father. The airplane is placed in front of the platform. After the naming and acceptance ceremony, it will proceed to the runway on the left for takeoff. The seats to the right of the stage are reserved for special guests and journalists. The seats to the left are for general guests and can accommodate thousands of people. Aircraft Specifications

The aircraft is a product of the Curtis Aeroplane and Motor Company of the United States. China has ordered twenty-eight aircraft from the company. Shanghai has eighteen, and various provinces have ten. All of them can be delivered within two months. The first aircraft to arrive is the Hawk fighter plane, which has a power of 700 horsepower and nine cylinders. It has a speed of 208 miles per hour and a ceiling of 31,000 feet. The front of the aircraft is equipped with two machine guns that can be fired simultaneously in the air. The belly can carry two rows of bombs that can be dropped individually or together.

Flight Performance

From 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM today, American aviator Major Doolittle will pilot the aircraft, departing from Longhua and flying over the city of Shanghai, scattering leaflets. Then, he will fly to the Jiangwan Racecourse. After this performance, American guests Kong Wu and Dwen Sun will fly airplanes borrowed from the Aviation Training Class of the Aviation Administration in Hangzhou. During their performance, one of them will jump from the plane and open the safety parachute strapped to his back, ensuring safety. The parachute is a product of the China Silk Weaving Company. It is said that the American performances are all on a voluntary basis, and the safety of those jumping from the plane will be their own responsibility.

Filming

The naming ceremony for the aircraft will be performed by Mayor Wu Tiecheng. The takeoff ceremony will be performed by Mayor Wu's wife. A chairman will be temporarily designated.
